    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2413978537" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2413978537" />
    <a title="Gumble&#39;s Yard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35482263-gumble-s-yard"><img alt="Gumble&#39;s Yard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604226927p2/35482263.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2413978537?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gumble&#39;s Yard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gumble&#39;s Yard" href="/user/show/35482263-gumble-s-yard">Gumble&#39;s Yard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781787330412" href="/book/show/36203391-my-year-of-rest-and-relaxation">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35482263-gumble-s-yard?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2413978537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7432425473208505170"><blockquote>
  <i>I was “on drugs.” I took upwards of a dozen pills a day. But it was all very regulated, I thought. It was all totally above board. I just wanted to sleep all the time. I had a plan. “I’m not a junkie or something,” I said defensively. “I’m taking some time off. This is my year of rest and relaxation.”</i>
</blockquote> <br/><br/>This novel is by Ottessa Mosfegh – author of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23453099.Eileen' title='Eileen by Ottessa Moshfegh' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eileen</a>, my views of which were neatly captured by the Sunday Times recent review of this book: <i>Billed as a thriller, Eileen was more of a mystery, a</i></span>
  <span id="freeText7432425473208505170" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>I was “on drugs.” I took upwards of a dozen pills a day. But it was all very regulated, I thought. It was all totally above board. I just wanted to sleep all the time. I had a plan. “I’m not a junkie or something,” I said defensively. “I’m taking some time off. This is my year of rest and relaxation.”</i>
</blockquote> <br /><br />This novel is by Ottessa Mosfegh – author of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23453099.Eileen" title="Eileen by Ottessa Moshfegh" rel="nofollow noopener">Eileen</a>, my views of which were neatly captured by the Sunday Times recent review of this book: <i>Billed as a thriller, Eileen was more of a mystery, a mystery as to how it ever got published, let alone garnered comparisons to Nabakov and wound up on the Man Booker shortlist.</i><br /><br />Eileen was one of a number of books (for example <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31213490.Sorry_to_Disrupt_the_Peace" title="Sorry to Disrupt the Peace by Patty Yumi Cottrell" rel="nofollow noopener">Sorry to Disrupt the Peace</a>) that spearheaded the “unlikeable female” narrator genre –relying on confrontational, unfiltered behaviour and calculated “grossness” (the first of which I can appreciate, the second of which always reminds me of nothing more than my experience in youth groups with young-ish children who think they can shock leaders by using swear words and sexual terms they have just learnt).<br /><br />My view of Mosfegh’s books was not assisted by a number of (again deliberately but childishly) provocative interviews she gave leading up to the award – in particular making it clear that she was nothing like her “loser” protagonist with a much more successful and fulfilled life. <br /><br />For balance though I have to say that by the time of the shortlist readings and book signings the author came across as intelligent and thoughtful. <br /><br />The unnamed narrator of this book lives in some privilege in her fully owned apartment in New York; although privilege earned by the successive deaths – from cancer and pill/alcohol suicide – of her parents; parents who were distant from each other and from her even during her childhood. <br /><br />She has an on-off, relationship with Trevor (a sado-masochist and commitment-phobe), works on the fringes of the New York art scene – in a conceptual art gallery – in late 2000/early 2001 but rejects much if not all of the lives she sees around her and takes refuge in drugs, alcohol and cynicism.<br /><br />Her only real "friend" is Reva. <br /><br />Reva’s (largely thwarted) aspirations are everything that the narrator is trying to escape: she is devastated by the cancer her mother is suffering; she is slowly climbing the corporate ladder, as an assistant at the insurance broker Marsh; searching for love – having an affair with her clearly manipulative married boss; obsessed with exercise classes, designer clothes she cannot afford and weight loss to the point of bulimia and declaiming (so often it becomes her signature phase) “no fair” at the narrator’s own natural slimness and beauty and inherited style (which the narrator reminds us about constantly). <br /><br />Reva’s weight obsession adds some humour to the book: getting pregnant by her lover (who immediately engineers her a promotion to her firm’s office in the World Trade Centre) she remarks <i>“The doctor said the abortion won’t cause any dramatic weight loss, but I’ll take it” </i> and after her mother’s death, wasted away by cancer: <i> “She probably weighed half of what I weigh now. Well, maybe not half exactly. But she was super skinny. Skinnier than Kate Moss, even.” </i><br /><br />Reva seems to take her beliefs and ideas from the trite and cliched world of Hallmark cards, lifestyle magazines and corporate mission statements – the narrator observations on Reva are (as one might expect from this genre) caustic and cruelly humourous: <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>I took a Polaroid of her one night and stuck it into the frame of the mirror in the living room. Reva thought it was a loving gesture, but the photo was really meant as a reminder of how little I enjoyed her company if I felt like calling her later while I was under the influence.<br /><br />After a minute or two of silence, she looked up at me and put a finger under her nose—something she did when she was about to start crying. It was like an Adolf Hitler impression. I pulled my sweater over my head and grit my teeth and tried not to laugh while she sputtered and whined and tried to compose herself. </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />But, more deeply, Reva’s life and attitudes somehow act as a remedy for the narrator’s malaise:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Reva scratched at an itch that, on my own, I couldn’t reach. Watching her take what was deep and real and painful and ruin it by expressing it with such trite precision gave me reason to think Reva was an idiot, and therefore I could discount her pain, and with it, mine. Reva was like the pills I took. They turned everything, even hatred, even love, into fluff I could bat away. </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />A remedy but not a panacea – and the narrator turns instead to sleep - the only shared activity she had with her mother. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>oh, sleep. nothing else could ever bring me such pleasure, such freedom, the power to feel and move and think and imagine, safe from the miseries of my waking consciousness. I was not a narcoleptic—I never fell asleep when I didn’t want to. I was more of a somniac. A somnophile. I’d always loved sleeping. It was one thing my mother and I had enjoyed doing together when I was a child. She was not the type to sit and watch me draw or read me books or play games or go for walks in the park or bake brownies. We got along best when we were asleep. </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />She locates a comically bad psychiatrist to assist her:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Try to sleep on your side when possible. There was recently a study in Australia that said that when you sleep on your back, you’re more likely to have nightmares about drowning. It’s not conclusive, of course, since they’re on the opposite side of the Earth. So actually, you might want to try sleeping on your stomach instead, and see what that does. </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Whose sole skills (but ones that are invaluable for the narrator’s purposes) are the ability to track down the latest drugs from internet articles and (more importantly) a fine judgement of how many, and at what frequency and quantity, she can prescribe without causing issues with health insurers.<br /><br />The narrator’s somnophilia causes her to lose her job (which she reacts to in a thankfully relatively rare outbreak of Eileen-style grossness by defecating on the floor of the gallery and stuffing the soiled tissues into the mouth of a stuffed dog forming part of an exhibition) and to take up systematically sleeping as a one-year sabbatical: <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>I was finally doing something that really mattered. Sleep felt productive. Something was getting sorted out. I knew in my heart—this was, perhaps, the only thing my heart knew back then—that when I’d slept enough, I’d be okay. I’d be renewed, reborn. I would be a whole new person, every one of my cells regenerated enough times that the old cells were just distant, foggy memories. My past life would be but a dream, and I could start over without regrets, bolstered by the bliss and serenity that I would have accumulated in my year of rest and relaxation.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />To her initial disquiet, she discovers a drug which rather than making her sleep seems to induce in her an extreme form of somnambulism – rendering her unaware of her actions for three days at a time<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>an unfortunate shift occurred. The carefree tranquility of sleep gave way to a startling subliminal rebellion—I began to do things while I was unconscious.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />But over time decides to embrace this as the culmination of her sleep experiment – and she strikes a deal with a conceptual artist from the gallery, who has access to paint her during the episodes in exchange for keeping her supplied for her intervals of lucidity. <br /><br />And unfortunately it is around this point that the book veers from, while not being exceptional, to at least being surprisingly (given its predecessor) promising into sheer tedium.<br /><br />Or at least this was my view – other readers may enjoy pages of lists of drugs and television programmes – so I include a very small sample:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>In the elevator back up to my apartment, I thought up combinations of pills that I hoped would put me out—Ambien plus Placidyl plus Theraflu. Solfoton plus Ambien plus Dimetapp. I wanted a cocktail that would arrest my imagination and put me into a deep, boring, inert sleep. I needed to 19 1 dispose of those photographs. Nembutal plus Ativan plus Benadryl. ........... I watched Driving Miss Daisy and Sling Blade. I took a Nembutal and drank half a bottle of Robitussin. I watched The World According to Garp and Stargate and A Nightmare on Elm Street 3: Dream Warriors and Moonstruck and Flashdance, then Dirty Dancing and Ghost, then Pretty Woman. </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />The book then culminates in an ending which was obviously foreshadowed throughout the book (and this review) – and really does very little with this idea other than with the closing words about a “jumper” <i>“There she is, a human being, diving into the unknown, and she is wide awake.”</i><br /><br />This book is I think meant to be around the sleepiness and then awakening of the New York art scene, up to and including 2001 – but did not really succeed for me at all. Some of the book is clearly a parody of conceptual art, but that is an art-form which is by its very nature self-parodying and does not need literary assistance.<br /><br />Another of the controversies around Eileen was the author’s admittance (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.theguardian.com/books/2016/sep/16/ottessa-moshfegh-interview-book-started-as-joke-man-booker-prize-shortlist">https://www.theguardian.com/books/201...</a><br />) that she wrote it using a guide to best seller fiction: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34657996.The_90_Day_Novel_Unlock_the_story_within" title="The 90-Day Novel Unlock the story within by Alan Watt" rel="nofollow noopener">The 90-Day Novel: Unlock the story within</a>. <br /><br />Good literature in my view needs ability, not how-to-write books, and tellingly this novel provides its own conclusion:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>I wanted to be an artist, but I had no talent,” I told her. “Do you really need talent?” That might have been the smartest thing Reva ever said to me. “Yes,” I replied. </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />My thanks to Random House for an ARC via NetGalley.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7432425473208505170" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3556827631" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3556827631" />
    <a title="Jean-Luke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9257436-jean-luke"><img alt="Jean-Luke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574623752p2/9257436.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3556827631?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jean-Luke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jean-Luke" href="/user/show/9257436-jean-luke">Jean-Luke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525522119" href="/book/show/36552920-my-year-of-rest-and-relaxation">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3556827631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6422668581806045359">In the middle of my copy of <i>My Year of Rest and Relaxation</i> I found a receipt for a bar tab totaling $213.00. Understandable. But had the receipt been dated 6/26/20 instead of 6/26/19, I would have said it makes perfect sense. Although it wouldn’t have been a bar tab (the bars were closed, remember—let’s do our best to forget the horror of it) but rather a receipt from the corner liquor store. Had we but known—<i>My Year of Rest and Relaxation</i> might have become a sort of how-to guide to getting thro</span>
  <span id="freeText6422668581806045359" style="display:none">In the middle of my copy of <i>My Year of Rest and Relaxation</i> I found a receipt for a bar tab totaling $213.00. Understandable. But had the receipt been dated 6/26/20 instead of 6/26/19, I would have said it makes perfect sense. Although it wouldn’t have been a bar tab (the bars were closed, remember—let’s do our best to forget the horror of it) but rather a receipt from the corner liquor store. Had we but known—<i>My Year of Rest and Relaxation</i> might have become a sort of how-to guide to getting through the year 2020. <br /> <br />Imagine Holden Caulfield pulling an Orlando and changing from male to female, and the resulting character might just be the main character in this book. The literary version of Charlize Theron in the movie <i>Young Adult</i>, or Harper in <i>Angels in America</i>, with some flashes of <i>The Devil Wears Prada</i> and <i>Bridget Jones’s Diary</i> and <i>RHONY</i>. <br /><br />As with Eugenides and the 1970s in <i>The Virgin Suicides</i> there is not a moment of doubt that this book is set firmly in the year 2000. I was 5 years old at the time so don’t laugh when I say it left me feeling nostalgic—I think all my childhood VHS tapes are still somewhere in my parents’ garage. This feels somehow wrong to write, but 9/11 made a very subtle and effective plot device.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6422668581806045359" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2228850103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16277287916129720229">This was bizarre and wonderful. I absolutely love Moshfegh's weirdness. She doesn't shy away from the things people usually hesitate to discuss, and she's fine with making her main characters off-putting. It's so refreshing to read. And that last page really took it all home. Like her other works, this novel will not be for everyone; but I think the people who like it will really like it. I sure did.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2451060741" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2451060741" />
    <a title="Meredith B.  (readingwithmere)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8930258-meredith-b-readingwithmere"><img alt="Meredith B.  (readingwithmere)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533786058p2/8930258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2451060741?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith B.  (readingwithmere)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith B.  (readingwithmere)" href="/user/show/8930258-meredith-b-readingwithmere">Meredith B.  (readingwithmere)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781787330412" href="/book/show/36203391-my-year-of-rest-and-relaxation">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2451060741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7021488265378384517"><b>4 Stars!</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>I am overcome by awe, not because she looks like Reva, and I think it's her, almost exactly her, and not because Reva and I had been friends, or because I'll never see her again, but because she is beautiful. There she is, a human being, diving into the unknown, and she is wide awake</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This was my first Otessa Moshfegh novel and it lived up to the hype. The cover threw me off as it almost has a historical fiction look to it but I will tell you that this is <u>not</u> anywhere near historical f</span>
  <span id="freeText7021488265378384517" style="display:none"><b>4 Stars!</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>I am overcome by awe, not because she looks like Reva, and I think it's her, almost exactly her, and not because Reva and I had been friends, or because I'll never see her again, but because she is beautiful. There she is, a human being, diving into the unknown, and she is wide awake</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />This was my first Otessa Moshfegh novel and it lived up to the hype. The cover threw me off as it almost has a historical fiction look to it but I will tell you that this is <u>not</u> anywhere near historical fiction.<br /><br />This is a story about a young twenty something, who I just realized never reveals her name as she's the narrator of this book - interesting choice by the author, who has everything and at the same time feels like she has nothing. She lives on the upper east side of Manhattan paid by her inheritance, but her parents are dead. She had a somewhat serious relationship with a guy on wall street but he dumped her for various reasons. She had a decent paying job but then got fired for being lazy. For every positive there's a negative and vice versa.<br /><br />This really is a story about a year of rest but not so much relaxation. The narrator starts to go to the worst psychiatrist that you could ever imagine and she completely over prescribes her medication but this is what the narrator wants. She wants her year of rest and relaxation to be just that - nothing but being blacked out and resting. Frankly, I have no idea how she didn't overdose, I guess her body was able to withstand 5-6 different kinds of drugs a day. The narrator takes us on this journey of her year where she has crazy therapy appointments just to get drugs, tries to get her ex back by threatening her life on the phone, pushing her "best friend" Reva away and ultimately just gliding through the year to restart.<br /><br />This is going to be hard to explain if you haven't read this book but <u>I completely understood and got what the narrator was trying to do and where she was coming from.</u> Her and I are complete opposites personality wise but throughout the story I was finding myself saying I can't relate but at the same time in a weird way I can relate to this. I think her end goal is the same as many of us: <i>sometimes we just want to start over.</i> Did she take it to the extreme? Yes, but everyone has their own journey and this was hers.<br /><br />I took some time to really think about this book while I was reading it and it helped reading it in small bits each night. Although there are some tough situations in this book, I felt the author did a good job getting me to understand the meanings behind what the narrator did. Yes, maybe she blacked out because of pills but I took that as sometimes we try to "black out" our feelings so that we can start over again.<br /><br />Maybe I'm making this more complex than it's supposed to be but this is what I got out of the book and overall I really enjoyed it! It is a work of fiction although I could see how some people may think it is non-fiction. I did chuckle a few times as well. Overall a solid read and I would recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7021488265378384517" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

She was recently lost both her parents, her father to cancer, and her mother close afterward from pills/alcohol.   <span id="freeText7273324943749925812" style="display:none">This is a book narrated by a very depressed and beautiful young woman who has graduated from college, works in an art gallery, and lives in New York, the year is 2001. She was recently lost both her parents, her father to cancer, and her mother close afterward from pills/alcohol. She also has an awful relationship with a man who is on again off again.<br />So... she decided she needs a year of rest, to just sleep for a year, consistently. She finds a psychiatrist who really is a horrible doctor, a pill pusher.. and gets everything she needs, more then she needs from her, and then we follow her through her journey ... along with her one friend Reva, a gal she was in college with and really the only friend mentioned besides the sometimes boyfriend.<br />Some of this is hilarious.... just a few laugh out loud moments, but the majority is very dark.<br /><br />Thank you to Netgalley and Penguin Press for the digital book.</span>

<div id="review_2566279399" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2566279399" />
    <a title="Henk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76202320-henk"><img alt="Henk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557871304p2/76202320.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2566279399?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Henk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Henk" href="/user/show/76202320-henk">Henk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789048846047" href="/book/show/41974787-mijn-jaar-van-rust-en-kalmte">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2566279399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15511601924812087773"><b>A hilarious, scathing account of lacking purpose and (not) dealing with depression. <br/>I loved the start but ended up a tad disappointed with the conclusion.</b><br/>While reading this book I constantly was reminded of this very short clip from an Avicii music video, where a psychiatrist responds to existential doubts with: "Let me get you some more pills"<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HUrGMTcSIlw'>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HUrGM...</a><br/><br/><i>I was finally doing something that really mattered. Sleep felt productive. Something was getting sorted out. I kne</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15511601924812087773" style="display:none"><b>A hilarious, scathing account of lacking purpose and (not) dealing with depression. <br />I loved the start but ended up a tad disappointed with the conclusion.</b><br />While reading this book I constantly was reminded of this very short clip from an Avicii music video, where a psychiatrist responds to existential doubts with: "Let me get you some more pills"<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HUrGMTcSIlw">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HUrGM...</a><br /><br /><i>I was finally doing something that really mattered. Sleep felt productive. Something was getting sorted out. I knew in my heart—this was, perhaps, the only thing my heart knew back then—that when I’d slept enough, I’d be okay. I’d be renewed, reborn. I would be a whole new person, every one of my cells regenerated enough times that the old cells were just distant, foggy memories. My past life would be but a dream, and I could start over without regrets, bolstered by the bliss and serenity that I would have accumulated in my year of rest and relaxation.</i><br /><br />The main character of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/44279110.My_Year_of_Rest_and_Relaxation" title="My Year of Rest and Relaxation by Ottessa Moshfegh" rel="nofollow noopener">My Year of Rest and Relaxation</a> is delightful despite her all encompassing apathy. Her goal is to sleep through her life, after her parents died. Something we can all relate to in the current horrorshow of a global pandemic and political polarization.<br /><br />We are taken to her life in New York, working for a modern art gallery, and her quest for a psychiatrist. Doctor Tuttle who turns out to be the most hilarious character ever, in a league with Sybill Trelawney from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5.Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban__Harry_Potter___3_" title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban (Harry Potter, #3) by J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</a> in terms of vague comments. Except she is a kind of drug dealer who helps our main character to go further and further. In the end this comes together in a kind of stasis where she is only awake an hour per three days. Her "life" is accentuated by an abusive boyfriend (who comes across as secretly gay and the personification of greed is good) and a girlfriend who is constantly dieting and complaining.<br />It is a story of a lack of purpose, a lack of genuine feelings, of being all exterior and material success (rich, blond, thin, educated) but still not being satisfied as a human being.<br /><br />The humor of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3276202.Ottessa_Moshfegh" title="Ottessa Moshfegh" rel="nofollow noopener">Ottessa Moshfegh</a> is delightful and her parody on the modern art scene, dieting, women judging each other and Big Pharma pushing opioids are all razor sharp, dark, unblinking and funny. Still, despite being dazzled by the skills of the author of turning a story without any real drive (rather the complete opposite) into a page turner, I was not really emotionally captured. Also the ending was something I saw coming quite early in the book. Still I am eager to pick up more from Ottessa Moshfegh.<br /><br />A lot of laugh out lot Dutch quotes below:<br /><br /><i>Mijn hoop was dat ik na een halfjaar winterslaap goed genoeg was genezen en immuun was geworden voor pijnlijke herinneringen.<br /><br />Ik was altijd opgelucht en geïrriteerd tegelijk als Reva plotseling opdook, zoals je je voelt als iemand je stoort terwijl je zelfmoord aan het plegen bent<br /><br />‘Ik wilde kunstenaar worden, maar ik had geen talent,’ zei ik tegen haar.<br />‘Heb je dat dan nodig?’<br />Dat zou weleens het slimste kunnen zijn wat Reva ooit tegen me heeft gezegd.<br /><br />Dagelijks mediteren heeft slapeloosheid bij ratten aantoonbaar verholpen.<br /><br />‘Ga je met de metro?’<br />In die periode ging ik elke dag met de metro naar mijn werk.<br />‘In zulke afgesloten openbare ruimtes gaan allerlei psychische ziektes rond. Ik voel dat jouw geest te poreus is.<br /><br />Reva had het vaak over huisje-boompje-beestje. Dat leek mij dodelijk<br />‘Ik blijf liever alleen dan dat ik iemands inwonende prostituee word,’ zei ik tegen Reva.<br /><br />Je bent te oppervlakkig. Dat bedoel ik niet verkeerd, hoor. Maar het is wel zo.<br /><br />We konden het beste met elkaar overweg als we sliepen.<br /><br />... en binnen no time zat ik zwaar onder de pillen en sliep ik de hele dag en de hele nacht met tussenpozen van twee of drie uur. Dat was nog eens goed, vond ik. Eindelijk deed ik iets wat er echt toe deed. Slapen voelde productief.<br /><br />Mijn lievelingsdagen waren dagen die ik bijna niet opmerkte.<br /><br />Ik vond dat hij eruitzag als een kinderverkrachter. Al die mannen zagen er zo uit. Maar dat gold voor iedereen in het juiste licht, leek me.<br /><br />Afwijzing, heb ik ontdekt, is de enige remedie tegen zelfbedrog.<br /><br />Ik vroeg me af of ik dood was, maar ik was niet verdrietig, alleen bang voor het hiernamaals, dat het volgende leven even saai zou zijn als dit.<br /><br />‘Ik ben als bevoorrecht persoon geboren,’ zei ik tegen Ping Xi. ‘Dat ga ik niet vergooien. Ik ben niet achterlijk.’<br /><br />Ik voelde de zekerheid van een werkelijkheid uit me gezogen worden, zoals kalk uit een bot. Ik was bezig mijn geest door uithongering in een staat van verwarring te brengen. Ik voelde steeds minder.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15511601924812087773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2696596311" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2696596311" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2696596311?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781787330412" href="/book/show/36203391-my-year-of-rest-and-relaxation">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=the-lost-girls">the-lost-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2696596311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13269549748231951022"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>The reviews of this book are hilarious. Half of them appear to be taking this book at face value, and the other half seem to be trying to come across as if they are op-eds for <i>The New Yorker</i>. MY YEAR OF REST AND RELAXATION is a polarizing book, and whether you'll like it depends on how you feel about reading depressing books with unlikable characters. If you want escapism and "soft" and "gentle" reads and joy, this book is going to go do</span>
  <span id="freeText13269549748231951022" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>The reviews of this book are hilarious. Half of them appear to be taking this book at face value, and the other half seem to be trying to come across as if they are op-eds for <i>The New Yorker</i>. MY YEAR OF REST AND RELAXATION is a polarizing book, and whether you'll like it depends on how you feel about reading depressing books with unlikable characters. If you want escapism and "soft" and "gentle" reads and joy, this book is going to go down about as well as, well, a dose of infermiterol.<br><br><br><br>MY YEAR OF REST AND RELAXATION is set in pre-9/11/2001 New York. The heroine is young, thin, beautiful, privileged, independently wealthy - and clinically depressed. She engages in a number of toxic behaviors, dating a user, befriending another woman who has an eating disorder and with whom she engages a highly co-dependent relationship, and spending all of her free time in bed or on her couch, watching old movies while taking drugs to "hibernate" and escape the uncomfortable intensity of her own emotions.<br><br><br><br>The narrator is jaded, selfish, and emotionally dulled. The portrayal of depression here is actually quite well done. People who have never experienced depression seem to think that it makes you cry and whine all the time (and, perhaps most unforgivably, willfully self-indulgent and done with agency), but for many people, there's a numbness and a feeling of hopelessness and despair: "What's the point?" you might ask, if nothing brings you joy and contentment, and you don't have the energy to do anything but sleep and eat and exist. When you're depressed, living isn't about enjoying the small things; it's about trying to muster up the energy to <i>do </i>the small things when you barely have the energy to get out of bed. Even though the heroine comes off as privileged, she is unable to enjoy any of the luxuries she has; the only solace she has in life is the escapism that comes from "dreamless" sleep. So what does she do? She engages a quack psychiatrist to feed her pill habit.<br><br><br><br>The psychiatrist is probably one of the most unlikable characters in the book (although the boyfriend, Trevor, is awful, too - having sex with your drugged-out unconscious ex? Yeah, buddy, that's rape). Dr. Tuttle is a crazy cat lady who has sessions in her nightgown and gives away free pill samples like they're fun-sized candy bars and it's Halloween. Some of the <i>NYT</i>-wannabe set were talking about this book being an existential satire, only I'm not sure what, exactly, MY YEAR OF REST AND RELAXATION is trying to parody. Is Moshfegh trying to go the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5206937-a-modest-proposal" rel="nofollow noopener">MODEST PROPOSAL</a> route in the vein of Johnathan Swift, suggesting that if #FirstWorldProblems sufferers want to use intoxication the way the population of <i>Brave New World </i>did with <i>soma </i>to escape from reality, then why not physically escape from reality by drugging yourself out and going into a coma-like hibernation state? The ending kind of suggests that, as if life itself is a dream and death is the awakening.<br><br><br><br>I found this book amusing and bemusing in equal parts. For most of it, I took the book at face value, as a depiction of depression that transcends class and circumstance. The heroine has a life that many would kill for - minus her dead parents - and has every opportunity in the world at her manicured fingertips, but because of her psychological state, it still isn't enough. That, I appreciated, because it's true that people can be depressed no matter how "happy" their life seems, and while depression is totally worse for people who don't have the resources or the safety net that a caring group of family and friends affords, that doesn't mean that being privileged means that you feel any less helpless.<br><br><br><br>It becomes harder to take this book at face value with the introduction of the walking malpractice suit that is Dr. Tuttle, the enabling solution she finds with avant-garde artist, Ping Xi, and the pill cocktails she takes on a daily basis that seem as though they should be causing some kind of physical harm or side-effects, especially since she mixes them with caffeine and alcohol. The human body is resilient, but not that resilient. I also disliked the ending, as I'm sure many of the people who rated this book so low did, as it <i>feels </i>like suicidal ideation. Here we have this character who describes their self-damaging behaviors as "saving herself," and when she witnesses death being committed with agency, she describes it as being awake; as if death was the solution to her problems all along.<br><br><br><br>MY YEAR OF REST AND RELAXATION isn't a bad book, and both the accolades and the criticisms are well-deserved, for various reasons. I fall in the middle here, because while I liked the book and found it interesting enough to continue, I didn't really like the end goal and I'm not sure what exactly the author was trying to accomplish with her message (if anything? maybe it was just a character study or an exercise in trolling the audience, and Ottessa Moshfegh is leaning back against the giant pile of money she got as an advance for this book and laughing at us all).<br><br><br><br>If you're depressed, you should probably avoid this book, as it will be triggering. It also deals with eating disorders, pharmacological abuse, suicide, addiction, and death. I'd read more from this author, but I wouldn't reread MY YEAR OF REST AND RELAXATION. It's a pretty miserable experience, even if it has some sharply cutting observation on the foibles and hypocrisies of humankind.<br><br><br><br>3 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="13269549748231951022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3313983990" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3313983990" />
    <a title="Tom Quinn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31467977-tom-quinn"><img alt="Tom Quinn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574458226p2/31467977.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3313983990?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom Quinn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom Quinn" href="/user/show/31467977-tom-quinn">Tom Quinn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781787330412" href="/book/show/36203391-my-year-of-rest-and-relaxation">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3313983990" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14858924751565826297">Tragically I'm not an undergrad anymore, so I will never be to be asked to compare and contrast this book with "The Yellow Wallpaper" in 2500 words or so. But still, Moshfegh's learnéd tone makes me yearn to put on the old critical reading hat and have a go. I am... compelled. Here, let me try and show you:<br/><blockquote>Reva had an interesting method of mixing her drinks. After each sip of Diet Mountain Dew, she'd pour a little Jose Cuervo into the can to take up the space her sip had displaced, so that by th</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText14858924751565826297" style="display:none">Tragically I'm not an undergrad anymore, so I will never be to be asked to compare and contrast this book with "The Yellow Wallpaper" in 2500 words or so. But still, Moshfegh's learnéd tone makes me yearn to put on the old critical reading hat and have a go. I am... compelled. Here, let me try and show you:<br /><blockquote>Reva had an interesting method of mixing her drinks. After each sip of Diet Mountain Dew, she'd pour a little Jose Cuervo into the can to take up the space her sip had displaced, so that by the time she finshed, she was drinking straight tequila. It was fascinating to me.</blockquote><br />First, this is a 100% relatable thing that I have done myself. But the scenes never stay at the surface, and Moshfegh also takes us through a bit of musing about Zeno's paradox, then unkind memories of a particularly toxic relationship, ending with the observation that "positive thinking is more powerful than negative thinking, even in equal amounts" - a deadpan delivered <i>by the bitch drinking the booze</i>, and pitched <i>to a girl attempting to self-narcotize into a permanent sleep</i> as an escape from life's anxieties. My symbolism sense is tingling!<br /><br />If any of this speaks to you, pick <i>My Year</i> up. The way Moshfegh arranges things, each little node amplifies the bigger signal by reflecting and reiterating the powerful feelings of contemporary malaise, high-functioning anxiety, first-world stress, and a weary need to escape. You can play fun games of literary analysis in how she gets there, searching for and ferreting out meaning. But then, while you're busy with all that academic bull, you'll get blindsided by a dirty joke or a casual description of some guy's dick which, hand to god and I kid you not, makes perfect sense in context.<br /><br />4.5 stars. Brilliant writer, love this voice, love certain passages for their hit-the-nail-on-the-head emotional resonance, but something is lacking - some sense of a bigger connection that stays just out of reach, some convalescence of the banal into redemption. All throughout I got whiffs of <i>The Stranger</i> and <i>The Awakening</i> and the literature of high society, but the story seems too frail to bear the weight of heavy analysis even as the energy leads me to try anyway. Maybe that's the point? Or part of it? I am an anxious person, and reading this felt at times crushingly familiar. I could have quit reading when it got uncomfortable but I continued on, because I felt... compelled. There's no cure for the human condition, there's no "escape" from life. There is daily management, at varying degrees of optimism, and there is a sense of relief in seeing that other people deal with this too, to validate that some elements of life are universal.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14858924751565826297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2154153793" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2154153793" />
    <a title="Blair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/272909-blair"><img alt="Blair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493499323p2/272909.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2154153793?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blair" href="/user/show/272909-blair">Blair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36418847-my-year-of-rest-and-relaxation">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=2018-release">2018-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=read-on-kindle">read-on-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2154153793" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11439643967684139874">The unnamed narrator of <em>My Year of Rest and Relaxation</em> may be obscenely privileged, but her life is bleak. She was neglected by her parents (both now dead), maintains an on-off relationship with a ‘reoccurring ex-boyfriend’ who treats her like shit, and has one friend, Reva, whom she despises. <em>‘I was plagued by misery, anxiety, a wish to escape the prison of my mind and body.’</em> In 2000, she begins a year-long process of ‘hibernating’ – staying inside her apartment in a narcotic haze, sleeping as </span>
  <span id="freeText11439643967684139874" style="display:none">The unnamed narrator of <em>My Year of Rest and Relaxation</em> may be obscenely privileged, but her life is bleak. She was neglected by her parents (both now dead), maintains an on-off relationship with a ‘reoccurring ex-boyfriend’ who treats her like shit, and has one friend, Reva, whom she despises. <em>‘I was plagued by misery, anxiety, a wish to escape the prison of my mind and body.’</em> In 2000, she begins a year-long process of ‘hibernating’ – staying inside her apartment in a narcotic haze, sleeping as much as she can. <em>‘Nothing else could ever bring me such pleasure, such freedom... safe from the miseries of my waking consciousness.’</em> She finds an eccentric psychiatrist who’s irresponsible enough to keep prescribing her every sedative on the market, month after month.<br /><br />It is, she claims, ‘the opposite of suicide’. She is obsessed with the idea that she will emerge from her hibernation a new person, a better person, all pain obliterated forever. <em>‘If I kept going, I thought, I’d disappear completely, then reappear in some new form. This was my hope. This was the dream.’</em> This irrational vision of rebirth does, in fact, sound a lot like a kind of suicide. Later, she will wonder, <em>‘what if the only way to sleep is death?’</em><br /><br />This is a repetitive story. Take drugs, watch videos, sleep, repeat. Wake up; piece together your movements from the detritus in your room. Lie to your terrible therapist. Pretend to listen to your terrible friend. Repeat, repeat, repeat. This was, surprisingly, something I liked about it. It’s a bold narrative choice, and it effectively mimics the way depression saturates everything with dread and makes you feel like you’re sleepwalking through a hopeless, pallid world. <br /><br />But, oh god, the tiresome misanthropy. The hateful obsession with women’s bodies. The moaning about how one’s overprivileged life has failed to meet one’s overprivileged standards. The amount of times the narrator unironically claims she ‘looks like an off-duty model’. The disgust with which she treats her best, and only, friend (who is also horrible, but humanised slightly by her blazing insecurity). The title character of <em>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23453099.Eileen" title="Eileen by Ottessa Moshfegh" rel="nofollow noopener">Eileen</a>
</em> was filled with hate – but at least she actually <em>was</em> downtrodden and poor and trapped in a horrible life. The narrator of <em>My Year of Rest and Relaxation</em> is rich beyond most people’s wildest dreams, lives on the Upper East Side, and is smart and beautiful. Not that any of this should necessarily mitigate her depression or loneliness, but it does make the bile she spews against others harder to stomach, especially when they’re worse off than she is, which they usually are.<br /><br />Books about unpleasant people behaving unpleasantly always walk a precarious line between brilliantly audacious and just, well, unpleasant. For me, Moshfegh’s debut <em>Eileen</em> was on one side of that line, and her short story collection <em>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29779229.Homesick_for_Another_World" title="Homesick for Another World by Ottessa Moshfegh" rel="nofollow noopener">Homesick for Another World</a>
</em> on the other; <em>My Year of Rest and Relaxation</em> lands somewhere between the two. Like <em>Eileen,</em> it is a brutally honest character study, unflinching and razor-sharp. Like <em>Homesick,</em> it is a draining reading experience (this might be fitting or ironic, depending on how deliberate you believe it to be) and, at its worst, it feels pointless.<br /><br />I had a strong reaction to some elements of <em>My Year of Rest and Relaxation,</em> which is why I needed to let it percolate, reread a few parts, to really see how good it is. Look at how perfectly the first chapter is structured – how it holds you fast from the first line. It’s irresistible and smooth and feels entirely effortless. When the book finds its momentum in the penultimate chapter, when the full scope of the narrator’s project is finally realised, it’s magnificent. When everything clicked into place I found myself feeling awed by it. This is a great novel, but like much of Moshfegh’s work, it is hardly ever likeable. <br /><br /><em>I received an advance review copy of</em> My Year of Rest and Relaxation <em>from the publisher through <a href="https://www.netgalley.com" rel="nofollow noopener">NetGalley</a>.</em><br /><br /><a href="https://tinyletter.com/learnthisphrase" rel="nofollow noopener">TinyLetter</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/learnthisphrase" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/learnthisphrase" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://learnthisphrase.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11439643967684139874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2495762189" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2495762189" />
    <a title="Meike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59050228-meike"><img alt="Meike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514995700p2/59050228.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2495762189?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meike" href="/user/show/59050228-meike">Meike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781787330412" href="/book/show/36203391-my-year-of-rest-and-relaxation">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59050228-meike?shelf=usa">usa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59050228-meike?shelf=2018-read">2018-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2495762189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18382098057547925827">I love how Ottessa Moshfegh embraces female characters who at first might seem unlikeable - she gives them a degree of psychological depth that makes it hard not to feel with them. Gradually, Moshfegh peels away the layers of defensive and outright weird behavior and the superficial self-explanations in order to expose what really drives these women - and just like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23453099.Eileen' title='Eileen by Ottessa Moshfegh' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eileen</a>, the unnamed protagonist of "My Year of Rest and Relexation" is struggling with trauma. <br/><br/>The young woman telling the story is </span>
  <span id="freeText18382098057547925827" style="display:none">I love how Ottessa Moshfegh embraces female characters who at first might seem unlikeable - she gives them a degree of psychological depth that makes it hard not to feel with them. Gradually, Moshfegh peels away the layers of defensive and outright weird behavior and the superficial self-explanations in order to expose what really drives these women - and just like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23453099.Eileen" title="Eileen by Ottessa Moshfegh" rel="nofollow noopener">Eileen</a>, the unnamed protagonist of "My Year of Rest and Relexation" is struggling with trauma. <br /><br />The young woman telling the story is a 26-year-old orphan who holds a degree in art history and works at a hip gallery in New York City. Locked up inside herself and shielded by cynicism, she is lonely, deeply depressive and feels stuck in her life. Her solution: She wants to find relief in extensive sleep, so she could be <i>"safe from the miseries of my waking consciousness."</i> After a year of hibernation, she figures, she'd be <i>"renewed, reborn"</i> - so at the core, she wants to sleep in order to be able to wake up from a life she experiences as nightmarish. When she finds a therapist irresponsible enough to prescribe her large doses of various sedatives, she starts her experiment. <br /><br />During the course of the book, we learn more about the sources of her depression, her parents, the NY art and hipster scene (I actually like those people, still I found the descriptions hilarious), her only friend, the insecure Reva, and her older on/off boyfriend Trevor, whom she loves although (or because?) he is not treating her well, to put it mildly. Piece by piece, we get a clearer picture of the protagonist.<br /><br />The way Moshfegh writes about drug abuse reminded my of Tao Lin's infamous <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23342903.Taipeh" title="Taipeh by Tao Lin" rel="nofollow noopener">Taipeh</a>, in which sedatives are also casually used to block out life. In Moshfegh's book though, the protagonist's fears and desparation feel a lot more plausible. And of course, Moshfegh is just a way, way better writer, her prose feels more urgent and she knows how to punch her readers in the face with her story. Both of them discuss people keen on numbing themselves though, and in times of the opioid crisis, it's hard to argue that this isn't topical literature.<br /><br />Apart from the importance of mildew in the text - everything seems in decay -, I'd also like to point out the role of Whoopi Goldberg (mentioned 23 times in the book!): <i>"Whenever she appeared on-screen, I sensed she was laughing at the whole production. Her presence made the show completely absurd"</i> - our protagonist can't laugh at the production that is her life, and by the end of her experiment, 9/11 will bring yet another twist. <br /><br />I see that Ottessa Moshfegh's books are not for everybody, but I have to say that I am fascinated by what she writes and what she aims to achieve.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18382098057547925827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3005008115" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Ines" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43642795-ines"><img alt="Ines" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542692123p2/43642795.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3005008115?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ines" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ines" href="/user/show/43642795-ines">Ines</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/46126661-il-mio-anno-di-riposo-e-oblio">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3005008115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10999142997834096386">For the first time on GR I decided not to give any rating but try to review the book only. I never thought to read it, but due to the insistence of the my oldest daughter, who giggling and listing all the interesting elements found in the reading, she thought well to hide the Kindle and a book that I gave priority in reading, to entice me to read the coveted in question....<br/>For once she is not mistaken 😅😅, let’s say quickly, that the content is equal to absolute zero, the narrative revolves aroun</span>
  <span id="freeText10999142997834096386" style="display:none">For the first time on GR I decided not to give any rating but try to review the book only. I never thought to read it, but due to the insistence of the my oldest daughter, who giggling and listing all the interesting elements found in the reading, she thought well to hide the Kindle and a book that I gave priority in reading, to entice me to read the coveted in question....<br>For once she is not mistaken 😅😅, let’s say quickly, that the content is equal to absolute zero, the narrative revolves around a girl with important psychiatric issues and addiction on neuroleptics and sedatives drugs to make any doctor stroke himself while reading, including myself...<br>The aspect that really brings all the honor and admiration to the writer, is this very clever ability to speak and describe nothing, or rather, a set of tiny descriptions of short and predictable activities, movements or actions of everyday life, all written in the form of a diary and served a period of one year.<br>But how does this author keep you attached to the book and describe all the dirty, fragile, and classic pathological cunning of psychiatrists? I don’t know, I just know that with me it worked......but I think of so many here among us. The ending then, leaves you dismayed and almost saddened by the event described.<br>PS: ( Moshfegh knows all the correct pharmacological manual for the various diagnoses, the thing surprised me and made me giggle a little with embarrassment, is that with mastery, she chose all the drugs in use and administered at the end of the 90s and now for newdrugs arrived on the market, no longer with frequency prescribed!!!)<br>Read it, but very carefully!😉<br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570507402i/28260427._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Per la prima volta su GR ho deciso di non dare alcuna valutazione ma unicamente tentare di recensire il libro. Mai avrei pensato di leggerlo, ma a causa dell' insistenza della figlia grande, che ridacchiando ed elencando tutti gli elementi interessanti trovati nella lettura, ha pensato bene di nascondermi il Kindle e un libro a cui io davo priorità nella lettura, per invogliarmi a leggere l'agognato in questione....<br>Per una volta non si è sbagliata 😅😅, diciamo in modo svelto, che il contenuto è pari allo zero assoluto, la narrazione gira tutta intorno ad una ragazza con importanti problemi psichiatrici e una dipendenza da neurolettici e sedativi da far infartuare qualsiasi medico, me compresa....<br>L'aspetto che porta veramente tutto l'onore e l'ammirazione per la scrittrice, è questa furbissima capacità di parlare e descrivere il nulla, o meglio,un insieme di minuscole descrizioni di picccole attività di movimento o azioni di vita quotidiana, sotto forma di diario, servite il un lasso di tempo di un anno.<br>Ma come fa questa autrice a tenerti incollata al libro e a descrivere tutte le zozzerie, fragilità, e le classiche furbizie patologiche degli psichiatrici? non lo so, so solo che con me a funzionato......ma penso a tanti qui tra noi. Il finale poi lascia sgomenti e quasi intristiti dall' evento descritto.<br>PS: ( Moshfegh conosce tutto il prontuario farmaceutico corretto per le varie diagnosi, la la cosa che ha stupito e mi ha fatto ridacchiare un pò con imbarazzo, è che con maestria, ti serve proprio farmaci veramente in uso e somministrati alla fine degli anni 90 e a causa di nuovi sul mercato, ormai non piu' con frequenza prescritte!!!)<br>Leggetelo, ma con molta precauzione!😉</span>

<div id="review_2472920549" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2472920549" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3482226-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571473870p2/3482226.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2472920549?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/3482226-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525522119" href="/book/show/36552920-my-year-of-rest-and-relaxation">review of another edition</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3482226-sarah?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3482226-sarah?shelf=tob-2019">tob-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3482226-sarah?shelf=not-for-me">not-for-me</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2472920549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5105782685305272002">2.5 rounded down<br/><br/>First off -- I think I should put out there that I am someone who does not *get* Moshfegh's fiction. I understand from reading a number of reviews that many find her books to be brilliant... I am not one of those people.<br/><br/>I should add that this is a lot better than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30079724.Homesick_for_Another_World' title='Homesick for Another World by Ottessa Moshfegh' rel='nofollow noopener'>Homesick for Another World</a>, which I absolutely hated. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34405666.My_Year_of_Rest_and_Relaxation' title='My Year of Rest and Relaxation by Ottessa Moshfegh' rel='nofollow noopener'>My Year of Rest and Relaxation</a> is very readable, amusing and shocking in equal measure... but I finished wondering what the point of it all is.<br/><br/>If you've read any revi</span>
  <span id="freeText5105782685305272002" style="display:none">2.5 rounded down<br /><br />First off -- I think I should put out there that I am someone who does not *get* Moshfegh's fiction. I understand from reading a number of reviews that many find her books to be brilliant... I am not one of those people.<br /><br />I should add that this is a lot better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30079724.Homesick_for_Another_World" title="Homesick for Another World by Ottessa Moshfegh" rel="nofollow noopener">Homesick for Another World</a>, which I absolutely hated. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34405666.My_Year_of_Rest_and_Relaxation" title="My Year of Rest and Relaxation by Ottessa Moshfegh" rel="nofollow noopener">My Year of Rest and Relaxation</a> is very readable, amusing and shocking in equal measure... but I finished wondering what the point of it all is.<br /><br />If you've read any review of this you'll know the premise - a young and privileged New York residing woman decides she wants to sleep for a year, and recruits an unhinged psychiatrist to prescribe her with a huge cocktail of pills to help her achieve her aim. The book then follows her throughout the year, culminating in a predictable ending (if you've picked up on any of the clumsy clues throughout the book).<br /><br />There are a couple of other supporting characters -- our unnamed narrator's only friend, Reva, another privileged young woman who only seems to care about losing weight (she's bulimic) and getting her hands on designer clothes. There are the Egyptians who work in the bodega where our protagonist buys her coffee, a peculiar artist called Ping Xi, and her ex - Trevor - who is a complete twat... you can probably guess that their relationship is pretty on/off and dysfunctional.<br /><br />So that's pretty much all that happens. Early on the narrator loses her job in an art gallery and then becomes more and more withdrawn from society. I won't go into too much detail about what follows this, as that makes up 75% of the rest of the book, but it ends up being pretty repetitive.<br /><br />Overall this wasn't terrible, it just didn't impact on me in any way whatsoever. I was engaged initially to see what her pill-popping would result in... but after a while I kind of just wanted it all to be over. It was funny at times, hence the extra half star I've awarded it. I finished this feeling a bit like I did on finishing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32871394.The_Pisces" title="The Pisces by Melissa Broder" rel="nofollow noopener">The Pisces</a> - like I needed a good shower. I guess that is an achievement on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3276202.Ottessa_Moshfegh" title="Ottessa Moshfegh" rel="nofollow noopener">Ottessa Moshfegh</a>'s part.<br /><br />If you're a Moshfegh fan then I'm pretty sure this won't disappoint. But if you're not, as my GR friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2367720704?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Will said</a>, this is not the book to change your mind.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5105782685305272002" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('c3LiJ6D+Yk0NrkUEvKzIFcN2nMqq89h6R6sX7Xgg9pZmwxO8ZWcfHK8dKkTzWLN57bb1Acmt8U/KN42oFVUjZA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }

A college student and aspiring writer, she devotes he<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText3847402669752861186\" style=\"display:none\">A sharply intelligent novel about two college students and the strange, unexpected connection they forge with a married couple.\n\nFrances is twenty-one years old, cool-headed, and darkly observant. A college student and aspiring writer, she devotes herself to a life of the mind--and to the beautiful and endlessly self-possessed Bobbi, her best friend and comrade-in-arms. Lovers at school, the two young women now perform spoken-word poetry together in Dublin, where a journalist named Melissa spots their potential. Drawn into Melissa\'s orbit, Frances is reluctantly impressed by the older woman\'s sophisticated home and tall, handsome husband. Private property, Frances believes, is a cultural evil--and Nick, a bored actor who never quite lived up to his potential, looks like patriarchy made flesh. But however amusing their flirtation seems at first, it gives way to a strange intimacy neither of them expect. As Frances tries to keep her life in check, her relationships increasingly resist her control: with Nick, with her difficult and unhappy father, and finally even with Bobbi. Desperate to reconcile herself to the desires and vulnerabilities of her body, Frances\'s intellectual certainties begin to yield to something new: a painful and disorienting way of living from moment to moment.\n\nWritten with gem-like precision and probing intelligence, Conversations With Friends is wonderfully alive to the pleasures and dangers of youth.&quot;<\/span>\n  <a Is it possible that the man she loved as a teenager—and who professed to worship only her—may be far different from what she has always believed?\n\nAlternating between Vanessa’s present and her past, My Dark Vanessa juxtaposes memory and trauma with the breathless excitement of a teenage girl discovering the power her own body can wield. Thought-provoking and impossible to put down, this is a masterful portrayal of troubled adolescence and its repercussions that raises vital questions about agency, consent, complicity, and victimhood. Written with the haunting intimacy of The Girls and the creeping intensity of Room, My Dark Vanessa is an era-defining novel that brilliantly captures and reflects the shifting cultural mores <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12767972849207346566">Ottessa Moshfegh is a fiction writer from New England. Her first book, <i>McGlue</i>, a novella, won the Fence Modern Prize in Prose and the Believer Book Award. She is also the author of the short story collection <i>Homesick for Another World.</i> Her stories have been published in <i>The Paris Review, The New Yorker,</i> and <i>Granta,</i> and have earned her a Pushcart Prize, an O. Henry Award, the Plimpton Discovery Pri</span>
  <span id="freeText12767972849207346566" style="display:none">Ottessa Moshfegh is a fiction writer from New England. Her first book, <i>McGlue</i>, a novella, won the Fence Modern Prize in Prose and the Believer Book Award. She is also the author of the short story collection <i>Homesick for Another World.</i> Her stories have been published in <i>The Paris Review, The New Yorker,</i> and <i>Granta,</i> and have earned her a Pushcart Prize, an O. Henry Award, the Plimpton Discovery Prize, and a grant from the National Endowment for the Arts. <i>Eileen</i>, her first novel, was shortlisted for the National Book Critics Circle Award and the Man Booker Prize, and won the PEN/Hemingway Award for debut fiction; <i>My Year of Rest and Relaxation</i>, her second novel, was a <i>New York Times</i> bestseller.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12767972849207346566" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

            <nobr>
              &mdash;

          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Sleep felt productive. Something was getting sorted out. I knew in my heart—this was, perhaps, the only thing my heart knew back then—that when I'd slept enough, I'd be okay. I'd be renewed, reborn. I would be a whole new person, every one of my cells regenerated enough times that the old cells were just distant, foggy memories. My past life would be but a dream, and I could start over without regrets, bolstered by the bliss and serenity that I would have accumulated in my year of rest and relaxation.&rdquo;</span>
